<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#ddd"><span style="font-weight:normal;"> <sup><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="525" height="8" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/7px-X_mark.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/11px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/14px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" width="7"/><span style="display:none">N</span><img alt="Yes" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="7" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/7px-Yes_check.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/11px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/14px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" width="7"/><span style="display:none">Y</span></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Chemicals/Chembox_validation" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Chemicals/Chembox validation">(what is this?)</a></span><span style="font-weight:normal;">  <span class="reflink plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:ComparePages&amp;rev1=443398218&amp;page2=Aripiprazole">(verify)</a></span></span></th>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Aripiprazole</b>, sold under the brand name <b>Abilify</b> among others, is an <a href="/wiki/Atypical_antipsychotic" title="Atypical antipsychotic">atypical antipsychotic</a>. It is recommended and primarily used in the treatment of <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bipolar_disorder" title="Bipolar disorder">bipolar disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHFS_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-AHFS-5">[5]</a></sup> Other uses include as an add-on treatment in <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">major depressive disorder</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tic_disorders" title="Tic disorders">tic disorders</a>, and irritability associated with <a href="/wiki/Autism" title="Autism">autism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> According to a <a href="/wiki/Cochrane_(organisation)" title="Cochrane (organisation)">Cochrane</a> review, evidence for the oral form in schizophrenia is not sufficient to determine effects on general functioning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coch2011_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coch2011-7">[7]</a></sup> Additionally, because many people dropped out of the medication trials before they were completed, the overall strength of the conclusions is low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coch2011_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Coch2011-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Side effects include <a href="/wiki/Neuroleptic_malignant_syndrome" title="Neuroleptic malignant syndrome">neuroleptic malignant syndrome</a>, a movement disorder known as <a href="/wiki/Tardive_dyskinesia" title="Tardive dyskinesia">tardive dyskinesia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hyperglycemia" title="Hyperglycemia">high blood sugar</a> in those with <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" title="Diabetes mellitus">diabetes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHFS_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-AHFS-5">[5]</a></sup> In the elderly there is an increased risk of death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHFS_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-AHFS-5">[5]</a></sup> It is thus not recommended for use in those with psychosis due to <a href="/wiki/Dementia" title="Dementia">dementia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHFS_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-AHFS-5">[5]</a></sup> It is <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_category" title="Pregnancy category">pregnancy category</a> C in the United States and category C in Australia, meaning there is possible evidence of harm to the fetus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHFS_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-AHFS-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> It is not recommended for women who are breastfeeding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHFS_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-AHFS-5">[5]</a></sup> It is unclear whether it is safe or effective in people less than 18 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHFS_5-6"><a href="#cite_note-AHFS-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is a <a href="/wiki/Partial_agonist" title="Partial agonist">partial</a> <a href="/wiki/Dopamine_agonist" title="Dopamine agonist">dopamine agonist</a>. Aripiprazole was developed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otsuka_Pharmaceutical_Co." title="Otsuka Pharmaceutical Co.">Otsuka</a> in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otsuka_Pharmaceutical_Co." title="Otsuka Pharmaceutical Co.">Otsuka America</a> markets it jointly with <a href="/wiki/Bristol-Myers_Squibb" title="Bristol-Myers Squibb">Bristol-Myers Squibb</a>. From April 2013 to March 2014, sales of Abilify amounted to almost $6.9 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thedailybeast.com_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-thedailybeast.com-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_uses">Medical uses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Medical uses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Aripiprazole is primarily used for the treatment of <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenia</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bipolar_disorder" title="Bipolar disorder">bipolar disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHFS_5-7"><a href="#cite_note-AHFS-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schizophrenia">Schizophrenia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Schizophrenia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The United States Food and Drug Administration approved the oral form of aripiprazole for the treatment of acute exacerbations of schizophrenia and for maintenance treatment (relapse prevention) in 2002. The approval was based on efficacy demonstrated in 5 "adequate and well-controlled" clinical trials, including 4 short-term studies ( 4 or 6 weeks) showing a reduction in psychotic symptoms in the acute setting and 1 longer-term study (26 weeks) demonstrating reduced relapse compared to placebo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Marketing approval was granted by the European Medicines Agency based on the results of these same studies, plus an additional long-term study demonstrating non-inferiority to haloperidol in the prevention of relapse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Health Canada approved aripiprazole for the acute and maintenance treatment of schizophrenia in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>A Cochrane review concluded that aripiprazole is similar to other typical and atypical antipsychotics with respect to benefit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coch2006_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coch2006-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Compared to typical antipsychotics, there are fewer extrapyramidal side effects, but higher rates of dizziness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="Updated version https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18646161 (September 2015)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> With respect to other atypicals, it is difficult to determine differences in adverse effects as data quality is poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="Updated version https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/24385408 (September 2015)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> A Lancet review found it is in the middle range of 15 antipsychotics for effectiveness, with better tolerability compared to the other antipsychotic drugs (4th best for weight gain, 5th best for <a href="/wiki/Extrapyramidal_symptoms" title="Extrapyramidal symptoms">extrapyramidal symptoms</a>, best for prolactin elevation, 2nd best for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/QTc" title="QTc">QTc</a> prolongation, and 5th best for sedation).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet2013_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet2013-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>A Cochrane review concluded that high dropout rates in clinical trials, and a lack of outcome data regarding general functioning, behavior, mortality, economic outcomes, or cognitive functioning make it difficult to definitively conclude that aripiprazole is useful for the prevention of relapse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coch2011_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Coch2011-7">[7]</a></sup> The authors concluded that for acute psychotic episodes aripiprazole results in benefits in some aspects of the condition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet2013_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet2013-17">[17]</a></sup> The World Federation of Societies for Biological Psychiatry recommends aripiprazole for the treatment of acute exacerbations of schizophrenia as a Grade 1 recommendation and evidence level A.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hasan_A.2C_Falkai_P.2C_Wobrock_T.2C_Lieberman_J.2C_Glenthoj_B.2C_Gattaz_WF.2C_Thibaut_F.2C_M.C3.B6ller_HJ_2013_2.E2.80.9344_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hasan_A.2C_Falkai_P.2C_Wobrock_T.2C_Lieberman_J.2C_Glenthoj_B.2C_Gattaz_WF.2C_Thibaut_F.2C_M.C3.B6ller_HJ_2013_2.E2.80.9344-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_for_Health_and_Care_Excellence" title="National Institute for Health and Care Excellence">National Institute for Health and Care Excellence</a> offers the following recommendations with respect to pharmacological treatment of those presenting with an acute episode of psychosis.</p>
<ul>
<li>Offer an oral antipsychotic medication.</li>
<li>Inform those who want to try psychological interventions alone that these are more effective when performed in conjunction with treatment with an antipsychotic medication</li>
<li>In the early post-acute period, warn the person of a high risk of relapse if antipsychotic medication is discontinued in the first 1–2 years after the acute episode</li>
<li>If a decision is made to discontinue medication, reduce the dose gradually and monitor for relapse for at least 2 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nice.org.uk_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-nice.org.uk-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The British Association for Psychopharmacology similarly recommends that all persons presenting with psychosis receive treatment with an antipsychotic, and that such treatment should continue for at least 1–2 years, as "There is no doubt that antipsychotic discontinuation is strongly associated with relapse during this period". The guideline further notes that "Established schizophrenia requires continued maintenance with doses of antipsychotic medication within the recommended range (Evidence level A)" <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barnes_TR_2011_567.E2.80.93620_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barnes_TR_2011_567.E2.80.93620-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The National Institute of Health and Clinical Excellence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nice.org.uk_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-nice.org.uk-19">[19]</a></sup> the British Association for Psychopharmacology<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barnes_TR_2011_567.E2.80.93620_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barnes_TR_2011_567.E2.80.93620-20">[20]</a></sup> and the World Federation of Societies for Biological Psychiatry suggest that there is little difference in effectiveness between antipsychotics in prevention of relapse, and recommend that the specific choice of antipsychotic be chosen based on persons preference and side effect profile. The latter group recommends switching to aripiprazole when excessive weight gain is encountered during treatment with other antipsychotics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hasan_A.2C_Falkai_P.2C_Wobrock_T.2C_Lieberman_J.2C_Glenthoj_B.2C_Gattaz_WF.2C_Thibaut_F.2C_M.C3.B6ller_HJ_2013_2.E2.80.9344_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hasan_A.2C_Falkai_P.2C_Wobrock_T.2C_Lieberman_J.2C_Glenthoj_B.2C_Gattaz_WF.2C_Thibaut_F.2C_M.C3.B6ller_HJ_2013_2.E2.80.9344-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bipolar_disorder">Bipolar disorder</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Bipolar disorder">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aripiprazole is effective for the treatment of acute manic episodes of bipolar disorder in adults, children, and adolescents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Used as maintenance therapy, it is useful for the prevention of manic episodes, but is not useful for bipolar depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Thus, it is often used in combination with an additional <a href="/wiki/Mood_stabilizer" title="Mood stabilizer">mood stabilizer</a>; however, co-administration with a mood stabilizer increases the risk of extrapyramidal side effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_depression">Major depression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Major depression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aripiprazole is an effective add-on treatment for major depressive disorder; however, there is a greater rate of side effects such as weight gain and <a href="/wiki/Akathisia" title="Akathisia">movement disorders</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spielmans_2013_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spielmans_2013-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid19687129_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid19687129-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid21154393_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21154393-29">[29]</a></sup> The overall benefit is small to moderate and its use appears to neither improve <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a> nor functioning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spielmans_2013_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Spielmans_2013-27">[27]</a></sup> Aripiprazole may interact with some antidepressants, especially <a href="/wiki/Selective_serotonin_reuptake_inhibitor" title="Selective serotonin reuptake inhibitor">SSRIs</a>. There are interactions with <a href="/wiki/Fluoxetine" title="Fluoxetine">fluoxetine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paroxetine" title="Paroxetine">paroxetine</a> and lesser interactions with <a href="/wiki/Sertraline" title="Sertraline">sertraline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Escitalopram" title="Escitalopram">escitalopram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citalopram" title="Citalopram">citalopram</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fluvoxamine" title="Fluvoxamine">fluvoxamine</a>, which inhibit <a href="/wiki/CYP2D6" title="CYP2D6">CYP2D6</a>, for which aripiprazole is a substrate. CYP2D6 inhibitors increase aripiprazole concentrations to 2-3 times their normal level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABILIFY_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-ABILIFY-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Autism">Autism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Autism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Short-term data (8 weeks) shows reduced irritability, hyperactivity, and <a href="/wiki/Stereotypy" title="Stereotypy">stereotypy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ching2012_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ching2012-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="Updated version https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/27344135 (December 2016)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> Adverse effects included weight gain, sleepiness, drooling and tremors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ching2012_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ching2012-30">[30]</a></sup> Long-term outcomes are not clear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ching2012_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ching2012-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Obsessive-compulsive_disorder">Obsessive-compulsive disorder</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Obsessive-compulsive disorder">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A 2014 systematic review concluded that add-on therapy with low dose aripiprazole is an effective treatment for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obsessive-compulsive_disorder" title="Obsessive-compulsive disorder">obsessive-compulsive disorder</a> that does not improve with SSRIs alone. The conclusion was based on the results of two relatively small, short-term trials, each of which demonstrated improvements in symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Side_effects">Side effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Side effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_side_effects_of_aripiprazole" title="List of side effects of aripiprazole">List of side effects of aripiprazole</a></div>
<p>In adults side effects with greater than 10% incidence include weight gain, headache, agitation or anxiety, insomnia, and gastro-intestinal effects like nausea and constipation, and lightheadedness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABILIFY_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-ABILIFY-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DM_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-DM-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMC_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-EMC-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMA_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Side effects in children are similar, and include sleepiness, increased appetite, and stuffy nose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABILIFY_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-ABILIFY-1">[1]</a></sup> A strong desire to gamble, binge eat, shop, and have sex may also occur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Uncontrolled movement such as restlessness, tremors, and muscle stiffness have been reported in children and adults, but they are rare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABILIFY_1-8"><a href="#cite_note-ABILIFY-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otsuka_Pharmaceutical_Co.2C_Ltd_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Otsuka_Pharmaceutical_Co.2C_Ltd-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discontinuation">Discontinuation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Discontinuation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/British_National_Formulary" title="British National Formulary">British National Formulary</a> recommends a gradual withdrawal when discontinuing anti-psychotic treatment to avoid acute withdrawal syndrome or rapid relapse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Joanne Moncrieff has suggested that the withdrawal process might itself be schizo-mimetic, producing schizophrenia-like symptoms even in previously healthy patients, indicating a possible pharmacological origin of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_illness" title="Mental illness">mental illness</a> in a yet unknown percentage of patients currently and previously treated with antipsychotics, but the limited evidence was found to support this hypothesis for antipsychotics other than clozapine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overdosage">Overdosage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Overdosage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Children or adults who ingested acute overdoses have usually manifested central nervous system depression ranging from mild sedation to coma; serum concentrations of aripiprazole and dehydroaripiprazole in these patients were elevated by up to 3-4 fold over normal therapeutic levels, yet to date no deaths have been recorded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skov_2015_41-44_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Skov_2015_41-44-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drug_interactions">Drug interactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Drug interactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aripiprazole is a substrate of <a href="/wiki/CYP2D6" title="CYP2D6">CYP2D6</a> and <a href="/wiki/CYP3A4" title="CYP3A4">CYP3A4</a>. Coadministration with medications that inhibit (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Paroxetine" title="Paroxetine">paroxetine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fluoxetine" title="Fluoxetine">fluoxetine</a>) or induce (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Carbamazepine" title="Carbamazepine">carbamazepine</a>) these metabolic enzymes are known to increase and decrease, respectively, plasma levels of aripiprazole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drugLabelWP_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-drugLabelWP-39">[39]</a></sup> As such, anyone taking aripiprazole should be aware that their dosage of aripiprazole may need to be adjusted.</p>
<p>For the purpose of D2 blockage, aripiprazole, a partial agonist on D2 receptor site, should not be used with a full antagonist.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources_(medicine)" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources (medicine)"><span title="Material near this tag needs references to reliable medical sources. (March 2014)">medical citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Precautions should be taken in patients with an established diagnosis of diabetes mellitus who are started on atypical antipsychotics along with other medications that affect blood sugar levels and should be monitored regularly for worsening of glucose control. The liquid form (oral solution) of this medication may contain up to 15 grams of sugar per dose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Patients with risk factors for diabetes mellitus (e.g., obesity, family history of diabetes) who are starting treatment with atypical antipsychotics should undergo fasting blood glucose testing at the beginning of treatment and periodically during treatment. Any patient treated with atypical antipsychotics should be monitored for symptoms of hyperglycemia including polydipsia (excessive thirst), polyuria (excessive urination), polyphagia (increased appetite), and weakness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pharmacology">Pharmacology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Pharmacology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Binding_profile">Binding profile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Binding profile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aripiprazole acts as an antagonist/inverse agonist (unless otherwise noted) of the following receptors and transporters:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Starrenburga_2009_164.E2.80.93170_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Starrenburga_2009_164.E2.80.93170-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drugLabelPC_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-drugLabelPC-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goodman_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Goodman-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid23469329_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid23469329-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid17897483_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid17897483-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid16135699_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid16135699-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid15592581_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid15592581-49">[49]</a></sup></p>

<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 24em; -webkit-column-width: 24em; column-width: 24em;"></div>
<p>Aripiprazole's <a href="/wiki/Mechanism_of_action" title="Mechanism of action">mechanism of action</a> is different from those of the other FDA-approved <a href="/wiki/Atypical_antipsychotic" title="Atypical antipsychotic">atypical antipsychotics</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Clozapine" title="Clozapine">clozapine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olanzapine" title="Olanzapine">olanzapine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quetiapine" title="Quetiapine">quetiapine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ziprasidone" title="Ziprasidone">ziprasidone</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Risperidone" title="Risperidone">risperidone</a>). Rather than <a href="/wiki/Receptor_antagonist" title="Receptor antagonist">antagonizing</a> the <a href="/wiki/Dopamine_receptor_D2" title="Dopamine receptor D2">D<sub>2</sub> receptor</a>, aripiprazole acts as a D<sub>2</sub> <a href="/wiki/Partial_agonist" title="Partial agonist">partial agonist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lawler_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-lawler-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-burstein_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-burstein-51">[51]</a></sup> Aripiprazole is also a partial agonist at the <a href="/wiki/5-HT1A_receptor" title="5-HT1A receptor">5-HT<sub>1A</sub> receptor</a>, and like the other atypical antipsychotics displays an antagonist profile at the <a href="/wiki/5-HT2A_receptor" title="5-HT2A receptor">5-HT<sub>2A</sub> receptor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jordan_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-jordan-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-shapiro-53">[53]</a></sup> It also antagonizes the <a href="/wiki/5-HT7_receptor" title="5-HT7 receptor">5-HT<sub>7</sub> receptor</a> and acts as a partial agonist at the <a href="/wiki/5-HT2C_receptor" title="5-HT2C receptor">5-HT<sub>2C</sub> receptor</a>, both with high affinity. The latter action may underlie the minimal weight gain seen in the course of therapy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid16336943_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid16336943-54">[54]</a></sup> Aripiprazole has moderate affinity for histamine, α-adrenergic, and D4 receptors as well as the <a href="/wiki/Serotonin_transporter" title="Serotonin transporter">serotonin transporter</a>, while it has no appreciable affinity for cholinergic muscarinic receptors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drugLabelPC_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-drugLabelPC-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>D<sub>2</sub> and <a href="/wiki/Dopamine_receptor_D3" title="Dopamine receptor D3">D<sub>3</sub> receptor</a> occupancy levels are high, with average levels ranging between ~71% at 2 mg/day to ~96% at 40 mg/day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kegeles_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-kegeles-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid12093598_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid12093598-56">[56]</a></sup> Most atypical antipsychotics bind preferentially to <a href="/wiki/Striatum" title="Striatum">extrastriatal</a> receptors, but aripiprazole appears to be less preferential in this regard, as binding rates are high throughout the brain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-editorial1_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-editorial1-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aripiprazole acts by modulating neurotransmission overactivity on the dopaminergic <a href="/wiki/Mesolimbic_pathway" title="Mesolimbic pathway">mesolimbic pathway</a>, which is thought to be the cause of positive schizophrenia symptoms. Due to its agonist activity on D<sub>2</sub> receptors, aripiprazole may also increase dopaminergic activity to optimal levels in the <a href="/wiki/Mesocortical_pathway" title="Mesocortical pathway">mesocortical pathways</a> where it is reduced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pharmacokinetics">Pharmacokinetics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Pharmacokinetics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Aripiprazole displays linear kinetics and has an elimination half-life of approximately 75 hours. Steady-state plasma concentrations are achieved in about 14 days. C<sub>max</sub> (maximum plasma concentration) is achieved 3–5 hours after oral dosing. <a href="/wiki/Bioavailability" title="Bioavailability">Bioavailability</a> of the oral tablets is about 90% and the drug undergoes extensive hepatic metabolization (dehydrogenation, hydroxylation, and <i>N</i>-dealkylation), principally by the enzymes <a href="/wiki/CYP2D6" title="CYP2D6">CYP2D6</a> and <a href="/wiki/CYP3A4" title="CYP3A4">CYP3A4</a>. Its only known active metabolite is dehydro-aripiprazole, which typically accumulates to approximately 40% of the aripiprazole concentration. The parenteral drug is excreted only in traces, and its metabolites, active or not, are excreted via feces and urine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drugLabelPC_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-drugLabelPC-43">[43]</a></sup> When dosed daily, brain concentrations of aripiprazole will increase for a period of 10–14 days, before reaching stable constant levels.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Aripiprazole was discovered in 1988 and Otsuka developed it independently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Independent_sources" title="Wikipedia:Independent sources"><span title="This claim needs a reference to a independent, third-party source. (November 2016)">third-party source needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Society and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulatory_status">Regulatory status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Regulatory status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It was approved by the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">Food and Drug Administration</a> (FDA) for schizophrenia on November 15, 2002 and the <a href="/wiki/European_Medicines_Agency" title="European Medicines Agency">European Medicines Agency</a> on 4 June 2004; for acute <a href="/wiki/Mania" title="Mania">manic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed_state_(psychiatry)" title="Mixed state (psychiatry)">mixed episodes</a> associated with bipolar disorder on October 1, 2004; as an adjunct for <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">major depressive disorder</a> on November 20, 2007;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> and to treat irritability in children with autism on 20 November 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Likewise it was approved for use as a treatment for schizophrenia by the <a href="/wiki/Therapeutic_Goods_Administration" title="Therapeutic Goods Administration">TGA</a> of <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> in May 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABILIFY_1-9"><a href="#cite_note-ABILIFY-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aripiprazole has been approved by the FDA for the treatment of acute manic and mixed episodes, in both pediatric patients aged 10–17 and in adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orangeBook_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-orangeBook-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, aripiprazole was approved by the FDA for the treatment of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unipolar_depression" title="Unipolar depression">unipolar depression</a> when used adjunctively with an antidepressant medication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> It has not been FDA-approved for use as monotherapy in unipolar depression.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Patent_status">Patent status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Patent status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Otsuka's US patent on aripiprazole expired on October 20, 2014;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-patent_5006528_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-patent_5006528-67">[67]</a></sup> however, due to a pediatric extension, a generic did not become available until April 20, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orangeBook_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-orangeBook-62">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Barr_Pharmaceuticals" title="Barr Pharmaceuticals">Barr Laboratories</a> (now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teva_Pharmaceuticals" title="Teva Pharmaceuticals">Teva Pharmaceuticals</a>) initiated a patent challenge under the <a href="/wiki/Drug_Price_Competition_and_Patent_Term_Restoration_Act" title="Drug Price Competition and Patent Term Restoration Act">Hatch-Waxman Act</a> in March 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> On November 15, 2010, this challenge was rejected by a <a href="/wiki/United_States_district_court" title="United States district court">United States district court</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Otsuka's European patent EP0367141,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> which would have expired on 26 October 2009, was extended by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supplementary_Protection_Certificate" title="Supplementary Protection Certificate">Supplementary Protection Certificate</a> (SPC) to 26 October 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The UK Intellectual Property Office decided<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> on 4 March 2015 that the SPC could not be further extended by six months under Regulation (EC) No 1901/2006. Even if the decision is successfully appealed, protection in Europe will not extend beyond 26 April 2015.</p>
<p>On April 28, 2015, the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) released a press announcement which approved the first generic versions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales">Sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2013, Abilify had annual sales of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>7 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dosage_forms">Dosage forms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Dosage forms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aripiprazole&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Perhaps owing to its mechanism of action relating to dopamine receptors, there is some evidence to suggest that aripiprazole blocks cocaine-seeking behavior in animal models without significantly affecting other rewarding behaviors (such as food self-administration).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid16806092_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid16806092-77">[77]</a></sup> Aripiprazole may be counter-therapeutic as treatment for methamphetamine dependency because it increased methamphetamine's stimulant and euphoric effects, and increased the baseline level of desire for methamphetamine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Urine drug screens are used to test for recreational drug use. There are case reports of 2 children accidentally ingesting large quantities of aripiprazole and subsequently testing positive for amphetamines on urine drug screens; both children then had gas chromatography-mass spectrometry analysis sent on their blood and urine that were negative for amphetamines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>

<li><a href="/wiki/Typical_antipsychotic" title="Typical antipsychotic">Typical antipsychotics</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Acetophenazine" title="Acetophenazine">acetophenazine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chlorpromazine" title="Chlorpromazine">chlorpromazine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chlorprothixene" title="Chlorprothixene">chlorprothixene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fluphenazine" title="Fluphenazine">fluphenazine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loxapine" title="Loxapine">loxapine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pimozide" title="Pimozide">pimozide</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vortioxetine" title="Vortioxetine">Vortioxetine</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>

<td colspan="2"></td>

<td class="navbox-list navbox-even" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><i>Unknown/unsorted:</i> <a href="/wiki/Ergoline" title="Ergoline">Ergolines</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Lisuride" title="Lisuride">lisuride</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pergolide" title="Pergolide">pergolide</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Piperazine" title="Piperazine">Piperazines</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Naphthylpiperazine" title="Naphthylpiperazine">naphthylpiperazine</a>)</li>
</ul>
